  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dcf504ee-a224-4222-a1e7-22d163d9b17a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText11847176945846193064" style="display:none">▶ <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37834816-ruin-and-rising" rel="nofollow noopener">Alternative Cover Edition #1</a>
</i><br /><br /><b>The capital has fallen.</b><br /><br />The Darkling rules Ravka from his shadow throne.<br /><br />Now the nation's fate rests with a broken Sun Summoner, a disgraced tracker, and the shattered remnants of a once-great magical army.<br /><br />Deep in an ancient network of tunnels and caverns, a weakened Alina must submit to the dubious protection of the Apparat and the zealots who worship her as a Saint. Yet her plans lie elsewhere, with the hunt for the elusive firebird and the hope that an outlaw prince still survives.<br /><br />Alina will have to forge new alliances and put aside old rivalries as she and Mal race to find the last of Morozova's amplifiers. But as she begins to unravel the Darkling's secrets, she reveals a past that will forever alter her understanding of the bond they share and the power she wields. The firebird is the one thing that stands between Ravka and destruction—and claiming it could cost Alina the very future she’s fighting for.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_35529926').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_35529926').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_35529926').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

    YES. Why do people think this was a satisfying ending? It was cliched, predictable and worse - it's mediocrity left me agitated. <br />I wish the author wou<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    YES. Why do people think this was a satisfying ending? It was cliched, predictable and worse - it's mediocrity left me agitated. <br />I wish the author would have come up with an ending that was .. darker and less predictable. A more unconventional happy ending or even an open ending would have been better.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_994594830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994594830" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994594830?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994594830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15495993530381975624">I AM SO PISSED. I AM SO PISSED.<br/><br/>Please allow me the indulgence of using an extended metaphor to describe this series.<br/><br/>The <b>first book</b> is the first stages of love. It's not true love, but infatuation. You are ensnared by his looks, enamored by everything he does. His quirks are adorable. His faults are overlooked because it's a part of who he is. It's part of what makes him special. So what if he has a habit of scratching his ass in public? It's cute.<br/><br/>The <b>second book</b> is the "settling in" stage of the</span>
  <span id="freeText15495993530381975624" style="display:none">I AM SO PISSED. I AM SO PISSED.<br /><br />Please allow me the indulgence of using an extended metaphor to describe this series.<br /><br />The <b>first book</b> is the first stages of love. It's not true love, but infatuation. You are ensnared by his looks, enamored by everything he does. His quirks are adorable. His faults are overlooked because it's a part of who he is. It's part of what makes him special. So what if he has a habit of scratching his ass in public? It's cute.<br /><br />The <b>second book</b> is the "settling in" stage of the relationship. You now see his faults, and they're pretty annoying. His habits of eating like a Neanderthal is now more annoying, less endearing. You really wish that he'd stop checking out other girls. You want to change him, but you are still in love, these are faults you can deal with because you're in this for the long run. The disappointments are inevitable in every long term relationship, aren't they? Over time, surely things will take a turn for the better.<br /><br />Or so you think. Until he dumps you without explanation.<br /><br />And so we come to <b>the third book</b>. It's 5 years since you guys broke up. He crushed your heart, left it in little pieces. You still love him anyway, despite what happened to end your relationship previously because there's just something about him. Some inimitable quality that attracts you and keeps you hanging on no matter what.<br /><br />And now he wants to meet again. You're excited. It's been too long. You've desperate with anticipation. This might be it. You guys might still have a chance.<br /><br />You wait in a cafe, in your best outfit, breathless with anticipation.<br /><br />And then he shows up. Time has not been kind. His hairline has receded by 2 inches. He has a paunch, and a double chin. He's grown a mustache that could only be described as a "douche-stache." <b>You had anticipated this</b>, but it still comes as a shock.<br /><br />Still, you can't bring yourself to hate him. You remember all the good times. You feel the sense of familiarity that you get with no one else, however much your physical attraction to him has changed. There's history between the two of you...and for now, that's the only good that came out of this meeting. You wish you had just left it there, where hopes and dreams and the flights of your imagination could have brought you more than this encounter ever could.<br /><br />That is my feeling towards this book. Grievously let down.<br /><br />I'll be happy to discuss the book. Please put spoilers in spoiler tags if you want to discuss in the comments =)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15495993530381975624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1418360945" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418360945" />
    <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader"><img alt="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550626778p2/8114361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader">Jesse (JesseTheReader)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418360945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5700220765303758233">That was an interesting conclusion to the trilogy. I can't say I'm super satisfied with how things came together, but it was still enjoyable! My main gripe with this series is it's lack of plot. I wanted more from the story, all three books feel like this build up to the ending, but nothing happens during those build up moments. (obviously this is just my opinion, you don't have to agree with me!) </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2756611778125371231">I feel like the entire trilogy could have been one book, not much happened at all</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466972745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8459947797360216253">Holy shit. This was brilliant and terrible and I have so many feels I can't even begin to describe.<br/><br/>Ok ok, listen. I know there are so many conflicting reviews on this book. But as for me? <b>I literally could not choose how I wanted it to end.</b> <br/><br/>I know, I might be a terrible person but I was totally OK with all three ending scenarios. At the beginning of this book, I was literally rooting for Alina to save the Darkling (or turn dark herself), Alina with Nikolai, and Alina and Mal. Ugh, I need all thr</span>
  <span id="freeText8459947797360216253" style="display:none">Holy shit. This was brilliant and terrible and I have so many feels I can't even begin to describe.<br /><br />Ok ok, listen. I know there are so many conflicting reviews on this book. But as for me? <b>I literally could not choose how I wanted it to end.</b> <br /><br />I know, I might be a terrible person but I was totally OK with all three ending scenarios. At the beginning of this book, I was literally rooting for Alina to save the Darkling (or turn dark herself), Alina with Nikolai, and Alina and Mal. Ugh, I need all three endings. I need them. I really, really need them.<br /><br />First of all, I freaking adore Alina. She was far from the perfect heroine, and by golly, I love her for it. She grew up and had an amazing character arc - yet still fought through so many weaknesses. Her arc is one of the most satisfying ones I've read in YA literature.<br /><br />But back to the ending - I gotta say I think Leigh Bardugo did the right thing, even though I so badly wanted to see the outcome of the other two. I don't want to give away spoilers and I get why somewhere upset but I can't help but think that there was no other truly appropriate endgame here. (Though I am still sad about the others...)<br /><br />So here it goes ... my little rants.<br /><br /><b> *****SPOILERS AHEAD.*****</b><br /><br />First and foremost, if you want a thread to sum up my Grisha feels, here it is.<br /><a href="https://twitter.com/glitzandshadows/status/1084075636786896896" rel="nofollow noopener">https://twitter.com/glitzandshadows/status/1084075636786896896</a><br /><br /><br /><u>MAL.</u><br />Poor Mal. He gets shit from everyone. Dude messed up, I agree. Maybe he isn't as alluring or entertaining as the other gents in this book, true. But the guy gave up his life for Alina in the end. Give him some credit. And no, for the record, I don't agree with those who claim he's abusive. He was jealous in S&amp;S and a bit of a poo head at times, and it got the best of him, but in the end, he did e v e r y t h i n g in his power to help her, whether that meant finding the stag to make her more powerful, or fighting to make sure she ends up a queen - he always fought for her. Always. Regardless of his feelings. And ya'll ... he ended up dying for her. <br /><br /><u>The Darkling's ...ending</u><br /><b>YES OK. I'm grieving, and I'll never get over him. Never. BUT.</b> Guys, he was a mass murderer and kinda deserved his end. Does that mean he is any less appealing? Lord save me, but nope. I love him. Best villain I've ever met. He'll always be one of my favorite characters but I refuse to rate this book just based off of those last few pages even though I shipped the hell out of him and Alina. I still do.<br /><br />In simple terms, he so badly wanted for her to be the one he could relate to, but before that, he wanted her for her power. Yes, they had so much chemistry, which totally altered his feelings if you ask me - but it doesn't change what he did to achieve his goals. <br /><br />(Also sign me up for any cat and mouse book because it's like... my favorite trope.) <br /><br /><u>Alina losing her powers</u><br />Yeah, I'm super sad about this too but I think it was the only way for Leigh to write her a happy ending. Do I wish it had been different? Totally. But from the beginning, Alina never wanted her powers. She was seduced by them later on, sure, but if you pay close attention to her narrative, she didn't want this burden. (But she became a badass either way.)<br /><br /><u>Nikolai</u><br />I literally cannot fit my feelings about Nikolai in a single review. Thank goodness he's getting his own series (after me begging for it since 2014). <br /><br />Also I read King of Scars. And I am dead bye.<br /><br />Anyway, I still can't rave enough about this series as a whole. <br /><b>All. Time. Favorite.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8459947797360216253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText8533993897863723480" style="display:none"><br><b>June 2019 update:</b><br><br>everybody stop liking this review i keep getting messages from ppl telling me why i thot this way like girl??? 😂 enough!!! let it rest already lol im tired<br><br>_____________________________<br><br>UPDATE Jan 2019:<br>i swear the more years pass- the more embarrassing this review gets lmao.<br><br>august 2018 update:<br><br>I have to admit, while Acomaf beat this ^ trash book in regards to storytelling, Acowar (Acotar #3) kinda sucked a lot so like... tread carefully and if anything- enjoy Acomaf only because I see that book as a standalone anyway.<br><br>Also, fuck this book &amp; the author lmfao.<br><br><b>UPDATE:</b><br>Okay so for those of you (like myself) who were disappointed with this ^ piece of trash- GO READ<br>"A COURT OF MIST AND FURY" in particular, I should say-- as the book really sets the stage and it beats this in every way and is everything r&amp;r could have been but miserably failed to be. <br><br>All the past angst and bitterness is beyond this spoiler tag.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>HEY LOOK WHATS UP</b> <br><br>MORE ANGST<br><br>I was talking to one of my tumblr friends a few days ago about some old wounds regarding this certain character who is like the other half of my dark heart and bad stuff that happened and then just this morning I was having a chat w/a GR friend about something related but it involved the angst over poorly written female protagonists and the boiling rage in the pit of my stomach over the lost potential of these certain protagonists. I was thinking this over in my head and I felt the need to apply a scenario to this one particular character(s) and notp that I (and a lot of my fellow friends) feel strongly negative about.<br><br>I was thinking of how Mal would be a <i>meninist</i> in the real world and he would be the kind of boyfriend that would be living in his girlfriend’s house and one night he’d just look at his amazing, successful girlfriend Alina and be like, <br><i>“Hey babe I just want you to know that I feel super uncomfortable by the fact that you make a lot more money than I do. And I also think that taking this route and that recent promotion you got, it’s just, it’s a bad idea. Maybe you should reconsider another job or just stay at home because I think that that power would corrupt you.”</i><br>When I apply this scenario with respect to the books, it goes like this:<br>Alina then suddenly feels terrible about how her boyfriend’s feelings are hurt and in turn she says, <br><i>“Hey I totally understand how you feel, I mean I wouldn’t want to ever feel worthless at all, like remember how I use to feel so shitty all those years ago before I got the job at this multimillion company and before you ever noticed me and became my boyfriend? I know what you’re going through and I wouldn’t want you to ever feel bad by something that makes me feel amazing. So you know what? I’m going to sell my house and we can go live in that rundown apartment that my aunt who used to hate me lived in before she died. At least we’ll be together and we can be equal and not have to worry about other things that might help us prosper in life.”</i><br><br>So now, lets apply this scenario to a way I prefer and think makes a LOT of sense and just sounds right:<br><br>After Mal gives his little bullshit speech, Alina runs off to get her wallet. She pulls out a hundred dollar bill from her wallet, reaches for a pen writes a few words on the bill. They read, <i>“You’re a piece of sexist garbage shit and not worth my time.”</i> Then she throws the hundred-dollar bill in Mal’s apparently flabbergasted face and tells him to get the fuck out of her house.<br><br>Then later that night as she’s lounging, she calls up her assistant Nikolai and tells him to connect her with CEO Morozova so she can accept his offer of promotion.<br><br>Just wanted to throw in all that angst. Sorry it sounds like such a badly written fic lmao. But hopefully my point is made. <br><br>...........................................................................<br><br><b>EDIT: 17/11/2014</b><br><br>Look. Me and a friend wrote a mini post- R&amp;R fic thing a while back on tumblr because we were depressed as hell. It's a little embarrassing sorry, bear with me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416278357i/11927059.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416278357i/11927060.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Me: <i>Aleks is sitting peacefully in a garden full of blooming flowers trying to have a peace of his mind when the distinct bunch of white orchids catch his attention and he is forced to burden himself with the thought of a little white haired stubborn girl living her life out someplace without him accompanied by a useless tracker who’s sudden thought makes Aleks contemplate ripping someones spleen out and he wonders if the new king would aid him in doing so since they were both cast aside by the summoner and he promises himself that throughout planning he would also get some flirting tips from the king and maybe even take his new flying vessel for a spin and perhaps crash it right on top of Keramzin and shout at the top of his lungs “SURPRISE BITCHES” and once thats done maybe even take over the world lmao byE.</i><br><br>Dani:<i> ORPHANS RUN SCREAMING FROM ALL EXITS, AND ALINA EXITS KERAMZIN BRANDISHING A BUTTER KNIFE AND A PASTRY CAKE GONE AWRY THAT IS TOUGH ENOUGH TO KNOCK A LESSER MAN OUT<br>"I KILLED YOU," SHE CRIES. ALEKSANDER GAZES DOWN AT HER, HANDS ON HIS HIPS AS HE SMIRKS.<br>"I BET YOU THOUGHT YOU’D SEEN THE LAST OF ME." while subtly checking her out because he is a lonely soul..</i><br><br>Me:<i>Alina’s hand tightens around the butter knife, still slick with the saints know what since she was actually never a doozy in the kitchen (probably would’ve been better at the summoner job but that went down the drain) “I’ve taken you down once, don’t think I won’t be able to again” she says.<br>Aleks squints at the pastry in her hand, “Not with that I hope. Looks deadly,” He mock smiles.<br>Alina frowns, “With the amount of sugar I put in it? Yeah, probably”<br>Aleks shrugs, “I have a sweet tooth.”<br>Alina’s eyes widen, “Oh, I didn’t know. You never told me.”<br>Aleks eyes almost threaten to bulge out of his sockets and he brandishes a hand at her in a taunting manner, loosing anger with every word “Really Alina? REALLY? Because last time I remember I tried talking to you (ok yeah I was pissed u turned me down for the sex BUT) even wheneva I tried talking to you, you FLEED OUTTA THE LIL PALACE LIKE THERE WAS SOME GODDAMN SALE AT IKEA SDFGHJASDASKJDKDSFFDSKJ ”</i><br><br>..........<br><br>GUYS I CAN'T FUCKING GET OVER THIS SHIT AHJAHSJKKALJSLKSADKLSDKSJDLSJKDL I HATE EVERYTHING<br><br>except Aleks<br><br><b>EDIT: 20/07/2014</b><br><br>yo fuck this book bro lmfao<br><br><br>EDIT: 06/17/2014<br><br>Im not going to lie man, Im heartbroken oof.<br><br>*Don't open this if you havent read R&amp;R*.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>you deserved better Aleksander.</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>..............................<br><br><b>alarkling teaser omg</b><br><br><i><br>“If only I’d known you’d prove such an apt pupil.” His voice was genuinely admiring, almost surprised. To my horror, I found that pathetic orphaned part of me taking pleasure in his praise. “Why come to me now?” he asked. “Has it taken you this long to recover from our skirmish?”<br><br>If that had been a mere skirmish, then we really were lost. No, I told myself. He’d chosen that word deliberately, to intimidate me.<br><br>I ignored his question and said, “I didn’t expect compliments.”<br><br>“No?”<br><br>“I left you buried beneath a pile of rubble.”<br><br>“And if I told you I respect your ruthlessness?”<br><br>“I don’t think I’d believe you.”<br><br>The barest smile touched his lips. “An apt pupil,” he repeated. “Why waste my anger on you when the fault is mine? I should have anticipated another betrayal from you, one more mad grasp at some kind of childish ideal. But I seem to be a victim of my own wishes where you are concerned.” His expression hardened. “What have you come here for, Alina?”<br><br>I answered him honestly. “I wanted to see you.”<br><br>I caught the briefest glimpse of surprise before his face shuttered again. “There are two thrones on that dais. You could see me anytime you liked.”<br><br>“You’re offering me a crown? After I tried to kill you?”<br><br>He shrugged again. “I might have done the same.”<br><br>“I doubt it.”<br><br>“Not to save that motley of traitors and fanatics, no. But I understand the desire to remain free.”<br><br>“And still you tried to make me a slave.”<br><br>“I sought Morozova’s amplifiers for you, Alina, that we might rule as equals.”<br><br>“You tried to take my power for your own.”<br><br>“After you ran from me. After you chose—” He stopped, shrugged. “We would have ruled as equals in time.”<br><br>I felt that pull, the longing of a frightened girl. Even now, after everything he’d done, I wanted to believe the Darkling, to find some way to forgive him. I wanted Nikolai to be alive. I wanted to trust the other Grisha. I wanted to believe anything so that I wouldn’t have to face the future alone. <b>The problem with wanting is that it makes us weak.**</b> A laugh escaped me before I thought better of it.<br><br>“We would be equals until the day I dared to disagree with you, until the moment I questioned your judgment or didn’t do as I was bid. Then you would deal with me the way you dealt with Genya and your mother, the way you tried to deal with Mal.”<br><br>He leaned against the window, and the gilded frame came into sharp focus. “Do you think it would be any different with your tracker beside you? With that Lantsov pup?”<br><br>“Yes,” I said simply.<br><br>“Because you would be the strong one?”<br><br>“Because they’re better men than you.”<br><br>“You might make me a better man.”<br><br>“And you might make me a monster.”<br><br>“I’ve never understood this taste for otkazat’sya. Is it because you thought you were one of them for so long?”<br><br>“I had a taste for you, once.” His head snapped up. He hadn’t expected that. Saints, it was satisfying. “Why haven’t you visited me?” I asked. “In all these long months?”<br><br>He stayed silent.<br><br>“There was barely a day at the Little Palace when you didn’t come to me,” I continued. “When I didn’t see you in some shadowed corner. I thought I was going mad.”<br><br>“Good.”<br><br>“I think you’re afraid.”<br><br>“How comforting that must be for you.”<br><br>“I think you fear this thing that binds us.” It didn’t frighten me. Not anymore. I took a slow step forward. He tensed but did not move away.<br><br>“I am ancient, Alina. I know things about power that you can barely guess at.”<br><br>“But it’s not just power, is it?” I said quietly, remembering the way he had toyed with me when I’d first arrived at the palace— even before, from the first moment we’d met. I’d been a lonely girl, desperate for attention. I must have given him so little sport.<br><br>I took another step. He stilled. Our bodies were almost touching now. I reached up and cupped his cheek with my hand. This time the flash of confusion on his face was impossible to miss. He held himself frozen, his only movement the steady rise and fall of his chest. Then, as if in concession, he let his eyes close. A line appeared between his brows.<br><br>“It’s true,” I said softly. “You are stronger, wiser, infinite in experience.” I leaned forward and whispered, my lips brushing the shell of his ear. “But I am an apt pupil.”</i><br><br>**she said the fucking word slakhbjadfksjlfs<br><br>................... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8533993897863723480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1980003795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1980003795" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1980003795?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=memorable-male-characters">memorable-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980003795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2782821752337392324"><b> 2 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b>	<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> Then he cupped my cheek, his thumb tracing my lip."You are all I've ever wanted," he said. "You are the whole of my heart.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491022146ra/22369245.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>^My face right now. <br/><br/>Let me preface this roast by stating-- <u>my problem isn’t the love triangle.</u> (If you can even call it that.) I’m not upset things didn’t turn out like I wanted, I’m frustrated the conclusion was a hot mess of nonexistent plot and unwinding character development. (Though I do obviously hate one of the love interests with all of my so</span>
  <span id="freeText2782821752337392324" style="display:none"><b> 2 Stars<br><br>Overview: </b>	<br><br><i>
  <blockquote> Then he cupped my cheek, his thumb tracing my lip."You are all I've ever wanted," he said. "You are the whole of my heart.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491022146ra/22369245.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>^My face right now. <br><br>Let me preface this roast by stating-- <u>my problem isn’t the love triangle.</u> (If you can even call it that.) I’m not upset things didn’t turn out like I wanted, I’m frustrated the conclusion was a hot mess of nonexistent plot and unwinding character development. (Though I do obviously hate one of the love interests with all of my soul)<br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696719383" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of Siege and Storm,</a> I theorized there were two possible outcomes for this trilogy—One where Alina embraces the Grisha society and uses her powers, and another where she rejects them and reverts to a ‘simple’ girl. I was <i>kinda</i> right? <s>Mostly wrong</s><br><br>My main problem is how <i>weak</i> a character Alina becomes. She had a fantastic amount of development in the first book, when she discovered her powers and started to believe in herself. The second book introduced a theme of greed, and hinted the way she used her powers would inevitably corrupt her. It’s probably the driving conflict of this <i>whole</i> book. <br><br>But it just flip-flopped back and forth before reaching a cop-out solution? It all works out spectacularly and everything is great, we can forget the past three books even happened????<br><br>Seriously, there was even the introduction of a third love interest so everything is <i>even</i> more complicated, and Alina has to choose between three entirely different lives. But somehow she hardly makes any decisions the whole book. <br><br><b> Pros: </b><br><br>Genya and David were beautiful. Baghara as Alina’s quasi-yoda was also a nice touch. <br><br>Nikolia’s humor and bravado was fantastic as always, and he was truly a bright-spot in this depressing book. <br><br>Bardugo’s writing is still very enjoyable. I flew through this, as the narrative flows easily and seems much improved from the first book. <br><br>The Darkling is super fascinating. Learning more about his backstory was one of the absolute highlights of this book, and his commanding presence made the pages he appeared 20x more interesting. He’s incredibly manipulative and cunning and there’s something so striking about his <i>confidence</i> in his actions. <br><br>I’m not discrediting his awful and abusive nature (and I do NOT support that romance) but he works brilliantly as an antagonist. <br><br><b> Cons </b><br><br>Mal was better, I guess? <s>I still hate him with the passion of a thousand suns.</s> He’s still outrageously ‘perfect’ and always says something mushy or has a completely selfless reaction to everything. He just doesn’t <i>feel real</i> to me. Even though he never noticed Alina before, he’s going to act like he’s always loved her and that his every action revolves around keeping her safe. <br> <br>There’s something <i>really</i> icky about the fact that he can’t accept her with her powers. Why did Alina keep making herself smaller for this guy?? It was like we were supposed to swoon over all the ‘sacrifices’ Mal made for her, though he spent the past three books whining about how much stronger she was than him?<br><br>What even was Nikolai the second half of this book, and was it necessary? <br><br>The pacing here was just… off. So much of this was filler or the characters standing in a circle talking about their course of action. I enjoyed the team-dynamic to an extent, but it cut a lot of tension out of things, in my opinion. Everything barely moved along, interlaced with a few dramatic scenes, before reaching a <i>very</i> rushed ending. <br><br>A very rushed ending that magically solves almost everything, undoes almost all the character development and was just… really lackluster? <br><br><b> In Conclusion </b><br><br>At least I can <i>finally</i> read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2782821752337392324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2540589804" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2540589804" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2540589804?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22718800-ruin-and-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2540589804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6045088111856654318"><i>”They will starve for you, lay down their lives and their children’s lives for you. They will make war without fear and die rejoicing. There is no greater power than faith, and there will be no greater army than one driven by it.”</i> <br/><br/>Three books and I still hate the Apparat! *lol* Guess that says enough about him and his despicable character. XD Despite everything he unfortunately has a point though. Now that Alina has become Sankta Alina for so many people they think that she’s the answer to all t</span>
  <span id="freeText6045088111856654318" style="display:none"><i>”They will starve for you, lay down their lives and their children’s lives for you. They will make war without fear and die rejoicing. There is no greater power than faith, and there will be no greater army than one driven by it.”</i> <br /><br />Three books and I still hate the Apparat! *lol* Guess that says enough about him and his despicable character. XD Despite everything he unfortunately has a point though. Now that Alina has become Sankta Alina for so many people they think that she’s the answer to all their prayers and hopes and to say this is quite a burden for a girl that considers herself to be ordinary isn’t even getting close to the truth. There’s a lot of pressure on our young heroine and even though she’s coping with it way better than she did in the past, this still doesn’t mean that she’s ready to do what is necessary. <br /><br />Mainly to destroy the fold and to dethrone the Darkling. To be entirely honest I can’t even blame her for it. The Darkling and her have some special connection and no matter how misguided he’s become, our favourite villain still has a good heart. It’s hidden more than just well in this final and last instalment but that doesn’t necessarily mean that it isn’t there. *sighs deeply*<br /><br />Also, am I crazy for still loving all those boys? *lol* Because no matter how much I think about it, I still like Mal, I still adore Nikolai and I still want more of the Darkling. XD And this after reading all three books! ARGH! Leigh why do you have to write such good characters? *lol* It’s just not fair! Well, anyway I’ll head to my characters section now because there is a lot I need to get off my chest and I don’t want to spoil you already! ;-P<br /><br /><b>The Characters:</b><br /><br /><i>”None of them were easy or soft or simple. They were like me, nursing hurts and hidden wounds, all broken in different ways. We didn’t quite fit together. We had edges so jagged we cut each other sometimes, but as I curled up on my side, the warmth of the fire at my back, I felt a rush of gratitude so sweet it made my throat ache.”</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>You are entering the Fold! If you don’t want to be spoiled or eaten by the volcra (which truth be told might be pretty likely) you better leave now. Don’t say I didn’t warn you! You’re entering at your own risk! *volcra howls in the distance* ;-P</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Alina:</b><br /><br /><i>”You are on your knees,” I said. “We are not negotiating.” <br />His lips thinned, but after a moment, he dipped his chin in assent.</i><br /><br />Okay, I admit it. Alina was pretty cool in this book! *lol* I loved how she decided to take her fate into her own hands and no longer aimed for compromises. It was all or nothing for her and I really, really liked this! For once she was no longer a chess piece in the game but turned into one of the leaders instead. <b>AND</b> I enjoyed it! XD It was about time she got her own voice and I’m glad she finally realized that it’s up to her to change things. Plus, if we’re entirely honest to run away never really worked out for her anyway! The Darkling would have never left her alone and it was about time she fought back. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”Maybe love was superstition, a prayer we said to keep the truth of loneliness at bay.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”This was what Ravka did. It made orphans. It made misery. No land, no life, just a uniform and a gun. Nikolai had believed in something better.”</i><br /><br /><b>Mal:</b><br /><br /><i>”For all my talk of vows and honor, what I really want is to put you up against that wall and kiss you until you forget you ever knew another man’s name. So tell me to go, Alina. Because I can’t give you a title or an army or any of the things you need.”</i><br /><br />Three books and I still don’t get all the Mal hate!!! I mean seriously, why do so many people hate him so much? I think he’s a really nice and down-to-earth guy and I could understand each and every single one of his actions. Yes he turned Alina away; he only did it because he knew she needed more than just a soldier who had nothing to offer though. In my opinion he was only realistic and let’s face it, if Alina wouldn’t have lost all her powers in the end she would have never been happy and content in a relationship with him. AND Mal was ready to sacrifice himself in order to save their world so I really, really don’t get why anyone wouldn’t like him!? I never had the feeling that he’s annoying, quite the contrary so yeah: <b>#IStillLikeMalAndI’mNotSorry</b><br /><br /><b>Nikolai:</b><br /><br /><i>”Saints, Alina. I hope you weren’t looking to me to be the voice of reason. I keep to a strict diet of ill-advised enthusiasm and heartfelt regret.”</i> <br /><br />OMG!!! If that is even possible I actually loved him even more than I loved him in book 2! Nikolai is the <b>BEST</b> and he deserves the world and so much more!!! &lt;333 I just admire and adore him and I really don’t get how Alina was able to resist his charms! I would have accepted his proposal in a heartbeat! *lol* But then again I’m not Alina who is obviously besotted with Mal. XD It made me kind of sad that we didn’t get all too much of him in this final book, but I see the logic behind it. <u>AND</u> I’ll never forgive the Darkling for what he did to my precious baby!!! I didn’t expect him to turn him into a monster and when it happened I was gripping my book so hard and yelling at the pages that I was very thankful I read it at home. *lol* (Just imagine I would have read it in the train… XD) I can’t wait to hold <b>“King of Scars”</b> in my greedy and grabby hands and I <u>
  <b>NEED</b>
</u> to know what happens next! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”Nikolai had made a fool of the Darkling, and now the Darkling had taken my polished, brilliant, noble prince and made him into a monster. Death would have been too kind.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He’d mobilized all the remaining units of the army to secure the borders, sent messages to the coast to rally Sturmhond’s fleet, and had apparently managed it all on no sleep and two fractured ribs. No one else would have had the ability, let alone the nerve – certainly not a younger son and rumoured bastard. But Nikolai had been training for this his entire life, and I knew he had a gift for the impossible.”</i><br /><br /><b>The Darkling:</b><br /><br /><i>”I have lived a long life, rich in grief. My tears are long since spent. If I still felt as you do, if I ached as you do, I could not have borne this eternity.”</i><br /><br />I might never forgive him for what he did to Nikolai but I still love him?! *lol* The Darkling is just one of those amazing villains I love to hate and despite everything he’s done there is still something good in him. His power and age made him ruthless and caused him to be detached from the world around him, but deep down in his heart he isn’t really bad. I guess you might say he is doing the wrong things for the right reasons. All he ever wanted was a united Ravka in which Grisha could live peacefully and together as one and for a while he even managed to give his country some sort of stability. He had a wonderful dream but he never realized that he became the one thing that stood in its way. The Darkling was a very complex villain and I’m so glad I read this series because villains like that are so rare to find. XD For that alone I’ll always cherish him. But that moment when he asked Alina to say his true name!? T_T I am deceased!<br /><br /><i>”Once more,” he said. “Speak my name once more.”<br />He was ancient, I knew that. But in this moment he was just a boy – brilliant, blessed with too much power, burdened by eternity.<br />“Aleksander.”</i><br /><br /><b>Genya:</b><br /><br /><i>”Na razrusha’ya. E’ya razrushost.” I am not ruined. I am ruination.</i><br /><br />Boy, did I adore Genya for her guts!! &lt;333 She stood up for herself and faced the king head-on and she didn’t just give him a piece of her mind but also accepted the consequences the truth might entail! <b>THAT WAS SO DAMN BRAVE</b> for so many different reasons!! I always knew why Genya is my Queen! XD I love that despite her scars she’s comfortable in her own skin and I’m so happy that she finally got the love she deserves! &lt;33 After everything she went through she deserves a man who treats her right and David seems to be the perfect man to give her everything she needs! ;-)<br /><br /><i>”Beauty was your armor. Fragile stuff, all show. But what’s inside you? That’s steel. It’s brave and unbreakable. And it doesn’t need fixing.” He drew in a deep breath then awkwardly stepped forward. He took her face in his hands and kissed her.</i> <br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; Mal:</u><br /><br /><i>”We’re going to be travelling together for who knows how long. Eventually, you’re going to have to talk to me.”<br />“I’m talking to you right now.”<br />“See? Is this so terrible?”<br />“It wouldn’t be,” he said, gazing at me steadily, “if all I wanted to do was talk.”</i><br /><br />I know at least 50% of the people who read this series will be all like “NOOOO!!!” now but: <b>I SHIP IT!!!</b> Yes, you read right! I’m happy with the ending and them being together! I mean Leigh made it pretty clear that Mal is Alina’s one true love and I’m so on board of the <b>“The childhood friend gets the girl”</b> train! *lol* Because this <u>NEVER EVER</u> happens in YA!!! And I’m grateful Leigh actually made it happen for once! XD It might sound ridiculous but this is something new and I’m always there for new things in a genre I already know so well. Plus Mal and Alina had a great chemistry and I loved that they were always able to joke about their situation. They knew each other inside out and for me it was logical that they could be together! I mean it’s basically like in real life. I know so many couples that started out as friends (some even best friends) and then became a couple because they realized they love each other. So there’s that! I ship it and I’m content with the ending! Enough said! ;-P<br /><br /><i>”All at once, the pain in my chest was so bad it nearly bent me double. Because this was what Mal had been coming to show me. Because that look – that open, eager, happy look – had been for me. Because I would always be the first person he turned to when he saw something lovely, and I would do the same. Whether I was a Saint or a queen or the most powerful Grisha who ever lived, I would always turn to him.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He watches her the way Harshaw watches fire. Like he’ll never have enough of her. Like he’s trying to capture what he can before she’s gone.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”I wanted more for you,” he said. “A white veil in your hair. Vows we could keep.”<br />“A proper wedding night? Just tell me this isn’t goodbye. That’s the only vow I need.”</i><br /><br /><i>”They had an ordinary life, full of ordinary things – if love can ever be called that.”</i><br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; Nikolai:</u><br /><br /><i>”First vomit, then tears,” Nikolai said, coming up beside me. “Don’t tell me I’ve lost my touch.”<br />“I’m just happy you’re alive,” I said, hastily blinking my eyes clear. “Though I’m sure you can talk me out of it.”</i> <br /><br />Their friendship was so amazing!!! I always knew they wouldn’t end up together but I loved that they developed such a great friendship in the end. They are proof that a friendship between a man and a woman can work just fine and their easy banter was so entertaining to read. If they would have married it would have merely been an alliance though and they both deserved better than that. I’m glad Alina can be with Mal now because I know Nikolai’s story isn’t over yet and I’m sooo curious to find out who’s going to be his love interest. XD A lot of people think it might be Zoya but I never saw chemistry between those two so there would have to be a lot of build-up in order to make that happen. Maybe Nikolai will even have a coming-out as being bi?! (I swear it could be possible!) Well, that certainly would be something I’d love to read. *lol* Whatever happens and no matter if it will turn out to be a straight romance or a gay one, I’m so ready for <b>“King of Scars”</b>!!! &lt;333<br /><br /><i>”I owe you, Alina. Ravka owes you. This and more. Do good works or commission an opera house or just take it out and gaze at it longingly when you think of the handsome prince you might have made your own. For the record I favour the latter option, preferably paired with copious tears and the recitation of bad poetry.”<br />I laughed.<br />He took my hand and pressed the ring into it. “Take it and build something new.”</i><br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; The Darkling:</u><br /><br /><i>”If only I’d known you’d prove such an apt pupil.” His voice was genuinely admiring, almost surprised.</i><br /><br />Ohhh I lived and breathed for their scenes! Their cat and mouse game was just too intriguing to read! They gave each other a run for their money and none of them yielded an inch! *lol* ARGH! Their relationship was so twisted and dark but damn was it awesome to witness! XD I think in a perverted way they both loved each other, but it just wasn’t enough to save the Darkling. It broke my heart that he had to die but the way Leigh wrote it I was okay with it. (Not like in “War Storm” when I was so damn disappointed about how it all ended …) The Darkling died with dignity and he died being loved by his opponent… It was a coherent ending and it was the ending he deserved. &lt;3<br /><br /><i>”It’s true,” I said softly. “You are stronger, wiser, infinite in experience.” I leaned forward and whispered, my lips brushing the shell of his ear. “But I am an apt pupil.”<br />His eyes flew open. I caught the briefest glimpse of rage in his gray gaze before I severed the connection.</i><br /><br /><i>”There will be nothing left,” I whispered.<br />“No,” he said gently as he folded me in his arms. He pressed a kiss to the top of my hair. “I will strip away all that you know, all that you love, until you have no shelter but me.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br /><b>“Ruin and Rising”</b> was a good and solid ending for a rather unconventional YA series! It kept me entertained and always caused me to wish for more. By the end of this book I got really attached to some of the characters and considering how many YA books I already read, that’s certainly no easy feat. ;-) So if you’re looking for a typical YA series that’s still able to surprise you every once in a while, <b>“The Grisha Trilogy”</b> is what you’re looking for. XD Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1126496181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126496181" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1126496181?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126496181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5492459471289724161"><b>*5 “you might make me a better man” stars*</b><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I will strip away all that you know, all that you love, until you have no shelter but mine.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><b>Agony. Pain. Tears. Heartbreak. Acceptance.</b> This is the way the Grisha trilogy ends.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435063100ra/15296920.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A masterpiece. A gem. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo' title='Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leigh Bardugo</a> gave everything she had in this grand finale. I'm numb and empty inside. I want to sit in silence and contemplate what happened and figure out the reasons why. I came to the conclusion that things were meant to end this way from the </span>
  <span id="freeText5492459471289724161" style="display:none"><b>*5 “you might make me a better man” stars*</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I will strip away all that you know, all that you love, until you have no shelter but mine.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Agony. Pain. Tears. Heartbreak. Acceptance.</b> This is the way the Grisha trilogy ends.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435063100ra/15296920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A masterpiece. A gem. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> gave everything she had in this grand finale. I'm numb and empty inside. I want to sit in silence and contemplate what happened and figure out the reasons why. I came to the conclusion that things were meant to end this way from the start. A battle of wills, <b>a battle between Light and Darkness</b>, self-preservation and sacrifice, greed and kindness, brain and heart.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I wanted to believe anything so that I wouldn’t have to face the future alone. The problem with wanting is that it makes us weak.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>After I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061957.Ruin_and_Rising__The_Grisha___3_" title="Ruin and Rising (The Grisha, #3) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin and Rising</a>, I faced the question <b>
  <i>how do I want to remember the Darkling</i>
</b>. He was a twisted, brutal tyrant, I could not possibly deny it and he proved it time and time again, each crime worst than the previous. But he was <i>more</i>. I choose to remember the brilliant dark haired boy, blessed with too much power, burdened by eternity, feared by his own kind, facing the entire world alone and wishing to change things, to create a place for the Grisha and himself. He was misguided, controlled by his greed and desires but this boy still <i>existed</i>, buried under layers of darkness. <b>I forgive him.</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“In the end, maybe love just meant longing for something impossibly bright and forever out of reach.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>There are so many other characters I want to talk about, but first I have to (grudgingly) admit that Mal <s>finally</s> won my respect, even though he's still my least favorite character. He understood his mistakes and what was at stake and it gave him a new perspective. I loved Zoya so so much, and David and Genya and Harshaw, and I'm so proud of Nikolai, the arrogant, all-too-clever fox who brought hope and laughter even in the most desperate times.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Na razrusha'ya.﻿ I am not ruined. ﻿E'ya razrushost﻿. I am ruination.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It was a fitting ending. <b>Suitable</b> I dare say, even though I hoped that some things would turn out differently. <b>So many plot twists and deaths that created a knot in your chest, desparation that threatened to drown you, mythical creatures, fanatic monks, flying ships, Saints and Demons, and in the center of the world-changing events, two orphans from Keramzin. </b>Who said that <i>otkazat’sya</i> aren't important?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5492459471289724161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2752453074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2752453074" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2752453074?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805094619" href="/book/show/37834816-ruin-and-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2752453074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7227208308175662590"><b>4.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“Na razrusha'ya.﻿ I am not ruined. ﻿E'ya razrushost﻿. I am ruination.”</blockquote><br/><br/>Look, I ain't gonna lie, <b>I finished this book two weeks ago</b> but hadn't had the time to write a good review about it (fuck you work) so I left it till this moment. And since then, because I'm a fucking goldfish, I don't remember shit. I delve into so many new stories each week, whether they may be tv shows, movies and books (obvs) that my mind is at its full capacity. My mind is 1tb and the fucking info is 5</span>
  <span id="freeText7227208308175662590" style="display:none"><b>4.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“Na razrusha'ya.﻿ I am not ruined. ﻿E'ya razrushost﻿. I am ruination.”</blockquote><br /><br />Look, I ain't gonna lie, <b>I finished this book two weeks ago</b> but hadn't had the time to write a good review about it (fuck you work) so I left it till this moment. And since then, because I'm a fucking goldfish, I don't remember shit. I delve into so many new stories each week, whether they may be tv shows, movies and books (obvs) that my mind is at its full capacity. My mind is 1tb and the fucking info is 587838tbs. Fuck off, mind, you're not a fucking hard drive, have more space! Anyway, let's start with the summary of the plot first, I hope I can remember something reading it.<br /><br /><i>The capital has fallen.<br /><br />The Darkling rules Ravka from his shadow throne.<br /><br />Now the nation's fate rests with a broken Sun Summoner, a disgraced tracker, and the shattered remnants of a once-great magical army.<br /><br />Deep in an ancient network of tunnels and caverns, a weakened Alina must submit to the dubious protection of the Apparat and the zealots who worship her as a Saint. Yet her plans lie elsewhere, with the hunt for the elusive firebird and the hope that an outlaw prince still survives.<br /><br />Alina will have to forge new alliances and put aside old rivalries as she and Mal race to find the last of Morozova's amplifiers. But as she begins to unravel the Darkling's secrets, she reveals a past that will forever alter her understanding of the bond they share and the power she wields. The firebird is the one thing that stands between Ravka and destruction—and claiming it could cost Alina the very future she’s fighting for.</i><br /><br />I remember myself being satisfied with this book, hence the rating. I didn't give the rating right now, I just remember, after having finished the book, this was the rating that was stuck in my mind. Not quite a 5 star, but more than the previous ones. Which seems to me like something positive.<br /><br />I remember (yes, I'm gonna start every fucking paragraph with a shitty I remember now, such a good reviewer I am) that the first part of the book and the middle were my least favorite. All the extreme and fanatic religious shit from the beginning left me wanting to leave the book down, for a moment. I was also confused about the whole situation, cause it seemed so different from the previous books. Thank God, it changed after that.<br /><br />I remember that I quite enjoyed the character development in this book. <b>Alina, Nikolai, Mal and the Darkling got major points for me after this book.</b> Even Mal. Yes, Mal. I think Mal kind of redeemed himself in this book, corrected his mistakes and was less arrogant and selfish. He's still my least favorite character, but I saw growth in him that I didn't think I would. Good on you, Mal. Also, the Darkling (I first wrote the Darling, oh my God) made me forgive him in this book. After everything, he's just a lost boy who was mislead and took the wrong path. <b>Alexander, I forgive you.</b><br /><br />I need to talk about Nikolai, <b>BECAUSE I LOVE HIM EVEN MORE!</b> There was so much less of him in this book, I WANTED MORE. When that thing happened to him... my soul was aching for him. I'm so happy for how everything turned out for his character, if I remember everything correctly. And I'm so glad it's not the end for this character, just the beginning.<br /><br />I will tell you the truth, I don't really remember why I saw character development in Alina. But I did, and that's important. I hated the fact though, that at the end Mal got what he wanted. <b>Alina with no powers and him in a position of power</b>. I wanted Alina to keep her powers, no matter who she would be with. <b>I would prefer Alina having her powers and ending up alone. That's the 100% fucking amazing ending for me.</b> But I guess this is an old book, shit was like this back then.<br /><br /><b>Oh Leigh, your world is still fantastic and so unique.</b> I'm so happy I get to explore this world again in many different more books, that for it to have stayed within this trilogy. I so can't wait to delve into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> duology. And then the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36307634.King_of_Scars__Nikolai_Duology___1_" title="King of Scars (Nikolai Duology, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">King of Scars</a> duology. <b>And the fucking NETFLIX SHOW.</b> Oh, Leigh, such a gem you have created.<br /><br />I have one major complain about this book... it still didn't make me truly care about the secondary characters. There were so many of them, and they weren't as developed as much as I would have wanted them to. <b>I think the story would be much richer, with a few more lovable and memorable characters.</b> Just my humble, little opinion.<br /><br />Overall, this was a more than adequate and fulfilling finale. My review wasn't as detailed as it should have been, I remember I wanted to say so many more things, but everything in my mind is fuzzy now and I wouldn't want to write something incorrect. I also, read most of this book on the train, while I was going to visit a friend, and it was soooo busy and noisy that many things flew over my head. Anyway, till the next one K BYE!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7227208308175662590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1626618408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626618408" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626618408?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626618408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5500185707240245628"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526840605i/25571252._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone</a> ★★★★★<br/>2.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626222536' rel='nofollow noopener'>Siege and Storm</a> ★★★<br/><br/>This book was a whole lot of ruin and not enough rising. <br/><br/><b>This review is going to have mild spoilers, especially with information about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626222536' rel='nofollow noopener'>Siege and Storm</a>, so please proceed with caution if you haven't read this trilogy. </b><br/><br/><u>Moral of this story:</u><br/>If you want the super hot guy you've been fantasizing about for years, make sure you never show that you can be more powerful than him in any aspect of your life. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385655901ra/7195565.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Mal wanted her powerless and he </span>
  <span id="freeText5500185707240245628" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526840605i/25571252._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> ★★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626222536" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> ★★★<br><br>This book was a whole lot of ruin and not enough rising. <br><br><b>This review is going to have mild spoilers, especially with information about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626222536" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a>, so please proceed with caution if you haven't read this trilogy. </b><br><br><u>Moral of this story:</u><br>If you want the super hot guy you've been fantasizing about for years, make sure you never show that you can be more powerful than him in any aspect of your life. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385655901ra/7195565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mal wanted her powerless and he got his wish in the end, because fuck women making men feel insecure, right? Who would want to be a queen when you could live a life in hiding, filled with mediocrity, with Mal? I mean, you probably will have lots of super hot sex, right? Obviously, the Darkling and Nikolai accepting her for who she really is was completely overrated. <i>/sarcasm</i><br><br>What makes me the saddest is that I actually thought this series would be different. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe love was superstition, a prayer we said to keep the truth of loneliness at bay.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>How could Leigh Bardugo create this literary masterpiece that is the Darkling and just completely throw him away? He was heads and shoulders above any other character in this series and we only get to see him five times in this book; one of those scenes being the biggest load of bullshit I've ever read. I have no words for my disappointment.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> was honest to God perfect for me, I chalked my disappointment with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626222536" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> to "Second Book Syndrome", but this book was an abomination. The ending made me feel like I completely wasted my time and that there was really no point in this series at all. <br><br>The most upsetting thing is that this could have been the best trilogy of all time<br><br>This world, these characters, and the potential were astronomical. I'm actually still dumbfounded how this happened because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386025950" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> was perfection, in my opinion. Maybe I'll feel differently once the bleeding stops, but I am just in disbelief by this <s>safe</s> terrible ending, when this could have been the next <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454172046?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454211563ra/17931388.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The only positive thing I'll say is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441209304?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> is, so far, amazing and I don't think it will turn out like this lackluster ending. I will stand by the fact that I believe <b>the Darkling is one of the best characters ever to be written</b>, so I'm just going to pretend that Kaz Brekker is the Darkling reincarnated, even though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441209304?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> picks right up where <i>Ruin and Rising</i> left off... I'm still going to pretend, because this is my coping mechanism!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450481818ra/17431808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will also say that Leigh Bardugo's prose is one of the most beautiful I've ever read, and it makes me want to read everything she creates, but I can't lie about the utter disappointment I felt when I finished the last page of this book. <br><br>Unfortunately, we got a generic ending to this trilogy with no twists that ultimately turned Alina into one of the weakest female characters I've ever read. I obviously wanted her with the Darkling with some kind of redemption story, but I would have even been happy with Nikolai. Instead we get Mal who should be dead, and not even because of the knife, but because I want to kill him myself for all of womankind. <br><br>I'm off to live the rest of my life through the Darkling fan-fiction. Goodbye, cruel world.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are all I’ve ever wanted,” he said. “You are the whole of my heart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5500185707240245628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
