    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2340343999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340343999" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340343999?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340343999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15008493653930750389">There’s a repeated problem within this novel where the time skips. The first book ends with the leads off to a new adventure. That new adventure is compromised and they are in the same old situation as before the finale less than twenty pages in. The second book ends with the lead characters in a bad situation. They are out of that bad situation less than forty pages into <i>this</i> book. It’s a <i>really</i> weird element and makes this story feel really unpolished. <br/><br/>Now, you might be thinking, <i>Elise, I love</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15008493653930750389" style="display:none">There’s a repeated problem within this novel where the time skips. The first book ends with the leads off to a new adventure. That new adventure is compromised and they are in the same old situation as before the finale less than twenty pages in. The second book ends with the lead characters in a bad situation. They are out of that bad situation less than forty pages into <i>this</i> book. It’s a <i>really</i> weird element and makes this story feel really unpolished. <br /><br />Now, you might be thinking, <i>Elise, I love you, but what the fuck does this have to do with anything?</i> Because it’s emblematic of a larger problem in the book: <b>
  <u>this book doesn’t know where it’s going.</u>
</b> <br /><br />This is a <i>deeply</i> weird book because it does not have a consistent tone or consistent character development or even, really, a consistent plot. It is a book with many interesting points and interesting characters and so many interesting themes and then the narrative doesn’t want to actually deal with that shit.<br /><br />➽➽First of all, let’s talk about Alina fucking Starkov. Because Alina is… such a complicated character and I don’t think that nuanced nature is being written very well. She’s so interesting because inwardly, she considers herself weak, but she’s playing with fire and desperately trying to avoid her own antiheroine nature. There are ways the nuance of her character can make sense, but <b>
  <u>the narrative isn’t very clear about her motivations and her struggles... until it’s convenient for the narrative to give her character depth.</u>
</b> <br /><br />➽➽Perhaps more importantly, the narrative is trying to <b>
  <u>force a conflict</u>
</b> out of her Being About To Go Bad. Which… we know isn’t happening. What antiheroine things does Alina do and think? Like, she complains a couple of times and… is sad, and then a couple of times per book, she threatens a guy with murder and it’s the most compelling she ever gets. Her narration doesn’t show us much at all of her desiring vengeance or Being A Power Hungry Antiheroine Badass; her primary motivation is usually a) being left alone or b) nonexistent. So we, as the audience, aren’t really afraid of her becoming a villain or turning bad. What’s the conflict here, then?<br /><br />➽➽Forced conflict is kind of a general problem within book two between Alina and Mal, and though it lessens a bit here, there’s still this underlying feeling throughout the books that… the obstacles between Alina and Mal really aren’t that big? Yes, they’re in vastly different walks of life and that’s causing resentment on his part, but it really gets boring seeing them play out the same patterns over and over again.<br /><br />➽➽<b>
  <u>Nothing character-wise really grows or changes throughout the entire fucking series.</u>
</b> I mean, think about Mal and Alina. Book one: Alina thinks Mal doesn’t like her back. Book two: Alina thinks Mal doesn’t like her back. Book three: Alina still thinks Mal doesn’t like her back, but also they can’t be together because... she thinks he doesn’t like her power back. But perhaps more importantly, think about Alina herself. Book one: Alina feels weak and not pretty enough, but also maybe she’s turning evil. Book two: Alina feels weak and not pretty enough, but also maybe she’s turning evil. Book three: Alina feels… maybe she’s turning evil. [But again, even if this weren’t repetitive, we as the audience don’t believe she’s turning evil!!]<br /><br />➽➽I said it in my review of book two, but as a general thought on this series: <b>
  <u>Leigh just will not let this get dark enough.</u>
</b> Alina makes for <i>such</i> a compelling antihero, but the only real motivation we see for her most of the time is a desire to be left alone. And that’s just not as compelling or interesting as her need for vengeance, her darker side. <br /><br />➽➽What was the plot? Where did it go? All they did was travel more and then I think the ending happened at one point maybe.<br /><br />✔✔I think the thing that really clearly improved in this book was the side character development. Tolya? Iconic. Nadia? Iconic bi. Tamar? Lesbian and iconic. Genya? So iconic. David? A good and totally iconic man. Zoya? Absolutely one of the most iconic characters in modern literature. Nikolai? I’d fucking give my life for Nikolai. I think this series gets that really good banter and those great character dynamics that I loved so much in Six of Crows, but watered down and we don't get enough of them because we're in Alina's head all the time. I really think Leigh Bardugo is meant to write multipov.<br /><br />So… let’s talk about the ending. Because it’s what everyone fights about. SPOILERS, obviously.<br />✔✔Alina ending up with the Darkling would have been kind of fucked up. That did not occur.<br />➽➽Did we ever resolve Alina's antiheroine shit? I don't think we did.<br />✔✔I guess she murdered someone and that was cool.<br />➽➽How the fuck did we resolve the Nikolai thing?<br />✔✔The epilogue was nice. It was. I really don't hate the ending. <br />➽➽I mean, it would have been cool if we resolved like, anything other than Alina's character?<br />✔✔y'all are going to kick me off Goodreads for this but I don't hate who she ended up with<br />➽➽But all that being said, Alina's character doesn't get the development needed for the ending to really make any sense or feel like a reasonable payoff for the character.<br /><br />Yeah, whatever. I'm giving this two and a half stars because it was somewhere between okay and I-liked-it. But I'm out here reading this review and realizing I didn't really like this all that much. It has a lot of narrative and structural flaws and the series as a whole has just been very consistently disappointing. Honestly recommend just skipping these for Six of Crows, the inventor of modern literature. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15008493653930750389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1192067964866170922" style="display:none">my original review wasnt much of a review, but more like an expression of awe. and gratefully, i still felt those feelings with this reread. so yes, my rating is very much based in nostalgia and personal bias. but man, this book (and series) is something else. <br /><br />i understand why reviews for this are mixed. where people saw filler, i read character development. and where others felt an imbalance of plot, i noticed the groundwork laid for character conclusions. so i guess what i am saying is the characters are what make this final installment shine for me. none of it would be worth anything if i didnt have such an attachment to them. <br /><br />so while i can acknowledge this isnt the most expertly written book/series out there, its one i adore and i know those feelings will remain for a long time to come. <br /><br />__________________________________<br /><br />i havent been this OBSESSED with a series (or author) in soooo long. you guys, i cant stop thinking about these books. how have i been able to live my life these past few years without knowing they existed?! i am truly blessed.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1037235626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1037235626" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1037235626?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=choking-noises">choking-noises</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=lolwut">lolwut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=could-have-been-worse">could-have-been-worse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=mayhem-and-misogyny">mayhem-and-misogyny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=lost-the-will-to-live">lost-the-will-to-live</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1037235626&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037235626" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1189035181035129166">If good high fantasy is a living body - blood pumping, juices flowing, joints moving, a hundred thousand tiny synapses and capillaries and white blood cells rushing and sparking and knitting together to form a natural machine - then this series is an empty ribcage, browned with age and disrepair. There are no lungs inside it; it doesn't creak and sigh with every nonchalant breath. It's just a pile of bones haunted by the ghosts of what it might have been. <br/><br/>Look, I knew this series would not go ou</span>
  <span id="freeText1189035181035129166" style="display:none">If good high fantasy is a living body - blood pumping, juices flowing, joints moving, a hundred thousand tiny synapses and capillaries and white blood cells rushing and sparking and knitting together to form a natural machine - then this series is an empty ribcage, browned with age and disrepair. There are no lungs inside it; it doesn't creak and sigh with every nonchalant breath. It's just a pile of bones haunted by the ghosts of what it might have been. <br /><br />Look, I knew this series would not go out with the sort of bang I enjoy (teehee) but I sort of expected more. What started as sort of a semi-cool concept devolved into another limp quest for magic objects that obviously is solved by the power of love or whatever. Yeah, I know this is high fantasy, but what makes high fantasy relatable and enjoyable is the realism in it. We're dealing with wars and revolutions and tyrants and our world, our real world, has had its fair share of wars and revolutions and tyrants. Those things aren't fantastical, so I expect them to be handled with a little more finesse. <br /><br />I give this book two stars because of Zoya, and the writing, which was okay. It's not Austen, but it'll do. It's better than <i>The Young Elites</i> which literally made me want to sleep for a year. It was so dead, it felt like ashes. It was so dead, it tried to suck me into the underworld.<br /><br />Alas, this book was a lacklustre ending to a series that I have already mostly forgotten about. It was kind of fun in the beginning, but grew more and more limp and tasteless, like lettuce that's been sitting out for too long. Actually, that's a good metaphor. Wilted lettuce. It once was crisp and juicy, but now it's a bad taste waiting to happen. <br /><br />Fin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1189035181035129166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1410746455235047919"><b>Read 2 | March 2019</b><br/><br/>I love rereading books and that onslaught of new and old feels. :') Also I'm so so glad I reread this because heck if I remembered even 15% which would've made King of Scars really awkward. (Also shout out to the fact that Nikolai got CALLED King of Scars in this on!! I wonder if the author planned it right from 2014 when she first wrote this?! We stan a foreshadowing queen.)<br/><br/>I definitely felt different things for this book than the first time. This time (1) I do think Mal/Alin</span>
  <span id="freeText1410746455235047919" style="display:none"><b>Read 2 | March 2019</b><br /><br />I love rereading books and that onslaught of new and old feels. :') Also I'm so so glad I reread this because heck if I remembered even 15% which would've made King of Scars really awkward. (Also shout out to the fact that Nikolai got CALLED King of Scars in this on!! I wonder if the author planned it right from 2014 when she first wrote this?! We stan a foreshadowing queen.)<br /><br />I definitely felt different things for this book than the first time. This time (1) I do think Mal/Alina needed to be shipped...lmao Nikolai deserves better anyway, (2) I was dubiously uninterested with like the first 60% and all the walking through caves, and (3) ok but I <i>actually care about the Darkling now</i>. A brilliant boy with too much power who let it corrupt him. I am just...! Like on second thoughts, I could read a prequel about him ok.<br /><br />I also lowkey forgot <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that Mal was the amplifier and ALINA STABBED HIM lmao. And I will forever be sour at how fast they moved on after Nikolai got cursed into a monstrous thing?!? Like as soon as he was gone, Alina and Mal started flirting hardcore. I was just. 0-0 where is the respect for my son. No one barely cared ffs.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧<br /><b>Read 1 | July 2015</b><br /><br />I've had a weird mix of feelings about this series. I liked the first book but...never felt emotionally engaged? But then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061955.Siege_and_Storm__The_Shadow_and_Bone_Trilogy___2_" title="Siege and Storm (The Shadow and Bone Trilogy, #2) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> was 5-star worthy. I fell in love with the world building and Nikolai and the magic and the science. But Ruin and Rising missed the heart I'd love from the first books. The beginning was too slow and I don't understand why people like the Darkling. He's weird and creepy and what's the pull?? And then I don't think it squandered some of it's more epic characters and just tossed them out in the end to serve minimal plot points<br /><br /><br /><br />*** EXCELLENT QUOTES ****<br /><br /><blockquote>"You never know," said Nikolai. "I've been busy. I might have some surprises in store for the Darkling yet."<br />"Please tell me you plan to dress up as a volcra and jump out of a cake."<br />"Well, now you've ruined the surprise." Thanks for teh rescue."<br />"Everyone needs a hobby."<br />"I thought yours was preening."<br />"Two hobbies."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I can think of a few more interesting ways to spend one's time."<br />"Is that supposed to be an innuendo?"<br />"What a filthy mind you have. I was referring to puzzles and the perusal of edifying texts." (pg 118) </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"You'll still make a great king."<br />"Of course I will," he scoffed. "I'm melancholy, not daft."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"If this stains my teeth orange --" said Zoya.<br />"It will," interrupted Genya, "but I promise to put your teeth back whiter than they were before. I may even fix those weird incisors of yours."<br />"There is nothing wrong with my teeth."<br />"Not at all," said Genya soothingly. "You're the prettiest walrus I know. I'm just amazed you haven't sawed through your lower lip." (pg. 216) </blockquote></blockquote></span>

<div id="review_560887150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/560887150?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=immortals">immortals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=editura-trei">editura-trei</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560887150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14368025970265837688"><b>REVIEW:<br/><br/>Actual rating: 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>So. I am conflicted. I initially gave <i>Ruin And Rising</i> 4 stars. After like half an hour of deliberating and second-guessing my rating, I switched it to 3 stars. If you'll ask me in a week, I'll probably say it was a 4 star read. So to be honest, I think it's a 3.5 from me. There are several reasons why I did this to the last book of one of my favorite series EVER and I'm gonna complain about every one of them, so if I start writing in CAPS, please understand that I'</span>
  <span id="freeText14368025970265837688" style="display:none"><b>REVIEW:<br><br>Actual rating: 3.5 Stars</b><br><br>So. I am conflicted. I initially gave <i>Ruin And Rising</i> 4 stars. After like half an hour of deliberating and second-guessing my rating, I switched it to 3 stars. If you'll ask me in a week, I'll probably say it was a 4 star read. So to be honest, I think it's a 3.5 from me. There are several reasons why I did this to the last book of one of my favorite series EVER and I'm gonna complain about every one of them, so if I start writing in CAPS, please understand that I'm about to combust from overwhelming feelings. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I will strip away all that you know, all that you love, until you have no shelter but me.”</b>
</i><br><br>I don't know why I gave it 4 stars in the beginning. I guess I'm loyal that way and I couldn't stand dishonoring this beloved series of mine, one I relentlessly recommended over and over. But I had to be honest with myself and admit there were things that bugged the hell out of me. Alina's missed big destiny she could've truly had. The lack of Darkling scenes. Mal's predictable role. And then there were things that balanced it out a bit. Baghra's and the Darkling's backstory -- finally!! The side characters, all awesome and, honestly, the only ones that developed in this installment. And, of course, Nikolai Lantsov, the prince of sass and strategy. <br><br>Alina sparked in <i>Ruin &amp; Rising</i> and showed me that she could be kick-ass, strong, manipulative and the no-bullshit-type. But this side of her vanished quickly and fizzled out altogether in the end. I expected her to be powerful, to have the destiny she deserved -- no, that she earned-- not just a happy-ending in the white-fence picket style. She could've been one of the major heroines in fantasy, but she settled for plain and ordinary and I know that for her it's enough. I understand her choices. I even somewhat respect them. But that doesn't mean I like them.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-64Bj12NQ7eI/U6aqPMLIJJI/AAAAAAAANmI/wAe0Xhz1AFI/s1600/poz%C2%A6%C3%A2+2.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403431739i/10092855._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“It’s true,” I said softly. “You are stronger, wiser, infinite in experience.” I leaned forward and whispered, my lips brushing the shell of his ear. “But I am an apt pupil.”</b>
</i><br><br>I want to gush over Baghra. I loved that woman! And I loved how she truly loved her son. There was a gut-wrenching scene that brought me to tears in which you could see the dynamic between her and The Darkling, how like calls to like and how you have to start taking action for making the changes you wish to obtain. Baghra also spilled out her secrets and I was pleasantly surprised it wasn't 100% what we (Grisha hardcore fans) previously guessed. And her story only increased my love for her, because she could be cruel, frustrating, sarcastic to no end, but she never tried to hide her flaws and mistakes. Just imagining living in such regret for hundreds of years, no one to share the burden with, made me question my own happiness and how... vain I felt in that moment. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EbJuP7fVYos/U6aqTiEmXVI/AAAAAAAANm0/LR9Kqh0Wnk4/s1600/tumblr_mcqpvofk3S1r7ksqyo1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403431739ra/10092856.gif" height="177" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“You want a love story too? There's none to be had.”</b>
</i><br><br>Now onto the complicated things. The guys. The Darkling was definitely my favorite character from The Grisha Trilogy. He's so multi-layered and complex, compelling and brilliant, dedicated and conflicting. His allure is always shocking, because his ruthlessness should make me scream <i>"The hell with him!"</i>. But no. The fact that he manages to make me teary eyed, although he's basically a killer spokes volumes of Bardugo's writing mojo. He's the best antagonist I've ever had the pleasure to encounter. You want to love him, to protect him, to hate him, to find out his every thought and secret and cheer him up once in a while. Yet the most gut-wrenching thing about him is how utterly alone he is. How he craves an equal. How he needs assurance that the world won't be just an empty vessel. And this whole revelation, along with his unraveled backstory, makes him so lovable in my eyes. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ivAIa6LyUEY/U6aqQ0y2ipI/AAAAAAAANmk/AeJtBVmZlzk/s1600/tumblr_inline_mhjkyrRok31qbu2m2.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403431739ra/10092857.gif" height="180" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“He was ancient, I knew that. But in this moment he was just a boy -brilliant, blessed with too much power, burdened by eternity.”</b>
</i><br><br>I liked Mal in this book far more than I did in the first two installments. You see, if I were to describe him in a few words, it would probably be determined, easygoing and a huge ungrateful ass. But my opinion about Mal changed quite a bit in this last book. For once, he finally realized how Alina's power is a part of her and that she doesn't need changing. She's special for who she really is and her talents bring out exactly that. He definitely became the main brick of support for Alina. And his stubborn determination and selflessness to help her in her war against The Darkling truly amazed me. Yeah, he might be a bit boring and a stuck-up prick whenever he wants to be, but he's also that cute, loyal and funny best friend that knows exactly what you want, need or fear. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jLrvrA581ns/U6aqQFpI7KI/AAAAAAAANmY/7svtwo7t9mY/s1600/poz%C2%A6%C3%A2+5.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403431739i/10092858._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nikolai was awesome and won major points in my overall appreciation for this book. His quick wit, his arrogance and love for clothes, his clever mind -- the Prince was a stand-up guy, not judgemental, always thinking about what's best for everyone. But guys, he had to endure some pretty sick stuff in this book and it made me proud to see him rise again afterwards, because if there's anyone who deserves to rule Ravka, it's him. There's also a scene in the first half of the book where he basically tells the King to go shove something up his ass and shut the eff up, or otherwise he'll charge him with rape. I don't think I've ever wanted to cheer and clap and yell "hell yes" so hard.<br> <br><i>
  <b>“Please tell me you plan to dress up as a volcra and jump out of a cake.”</b>
</i><br><br>The secondary characters were incredible! Genya, oh how much I loved her! She is awesome and she is fully appreciated in R&amp;R. I liked how strong she managed to remain through her tragic life story, with the same "I rock" demeanor, but the best thing of all? Her relationship with David. To see him finally stand up for Genya was simply clap-worthy. You're the man, David. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Beauty was your armor. Fragile stuff, all show. But what's inside you? That's steel. It's brave and unbreakable. And it doesn't need fixing.”</b>
</i><br><br>Is it impossible to believe I really liked Zoya? She's such a strong, sassy and unpredictable character! I think the biggest surprise was how much I constantly awaited the scenes with her. Plus, her one-liners were bazinga. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Maybe you’re hungry,” said Zoya. “I always get mean when I’m hungry.”<br>“Are you hungry all the time?” asked Harshaw.”</b>
</i><br><br>In addition to them, the twins were badass and compelling. They offered some funny release while staying loyal to Alina and being a very important asset to their goal. Harshaw was an okay character, but I felt we barely scratched the surface of his personality. Nadia and Adrik were interesting enough and Adrik's crush on Zoya was so sweet!<br> <br>You know my biggest regret about R&amp;R? No, sorry, make it the second. No, the third. Errr, maybe the fifth. Anyway -- The Apparat's ass wasn't handed over to him. Really, someone needed to show him who the real boss was so he'd lose the whole diva attitude. <br><br>About the ending... It broke my heart. I might've even shed a few tears. I refused to believe it was happening. Some will say it was perfect. Some will hate it with every fiber of their being. For me? It was bittersweet. Good things happened, bad things happened, but that's life so I don't have the right to complain. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ONN00sBtkCA/U6aqOteQLuI/AAAAAAAANmA/mF5ah6KH-R8/s1600/poz%C2%A6%C3%A2+1.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403431739i/10092859._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The romance might prove tricky to explain. Since we have quite a love, um, square, there was never a solid chance that we'll know who Alina would end up with. But I also wanted a different love story. One enchanting, complicated, defying and different. But I guess I have to look somewhere else for something that isn't prone to the same style of happy-endings. Le sigh. I don't want to spoil anyone, but I'm sure you can see I'm not quite happy about the endgame pair. And don't get me wrong -- I don't hate who Alina ends up with, I just thought that she'd be at her best with someone else. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-M1di__9fFY0/U6aqRXulH9I/AAAAAAAANmo/K6xApc_F2Cc/s1600/tumblr_m5p38jxuVj1rn95k2o1_250.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403431739ra/10092860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“It was something no other Grisha understood, and in the end, it was what bound the Darkling and me most closely—not our powers, not the strangeness of them, not that we were both aberrations, if not abominations. It was our knowledge of the forbidden, our desire for more.”</b>
</i><br><br>Anyway, I appreciate and respect that Alina finally got the happy-ending she wanted. She's content, she has friends that she can call family and she's surrounded by everything she's ever loved. <i>*squishes her in a hug*</i> <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4VkEQY_ruMs/U6aqPixuwSI/AAAAAAAANmU/adqKr_GRrNk/s1600/poz%C2%A6%C3%A2+4.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403431739i/10092861._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“A lesser Saint,” he said. “But perhaps a better queen.”</b>
</i><br><br>This book was good, but I expected it to be grand. I don't know -- maybe I was way too involved and my expectations were way above the clouds, but there's no way I can be objective when it comes to the ending of one of my favorite series. Yeah, it gave closure and it tied loose ends narratively speaking, but after reading R&amp;R I felt disappointed, sad and, to be honest, bitter. Because the fans' theories were better than the path Bardugo chose. Because this had so much potential for awesomeness and while it was still well written and interesting, it sort of failed to deliver the shock and amazement I've expected. Because R&amp;R ended up being quite a cliche-ish finale. Because it was somewhat predictable (good guesses, Grisha fans). <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UX5gb3PZZJE/U6aqUW83iDI/AAAAAAAANm8/Ak2PEZ2pzfY/s1600/tumblr_me3ocvLMpp1ryb0hd.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403431739ra/10092862.gif" height="180" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Maybe I could've overlooked how it ended and maybe I wouldn't be willing to pay someone to re-write it to my peculiar tastes (joking... I think) if it weren't for a slight issue. I was bored. Seriously. I found myself taking breaks from reading so I can avoid continuing it. But the need to know how it all clicked together won and I caved in to my greedy heart. <br><br>I'll still read anything Leigh Bardugo writes. She's awesome like that and has killer writing skills, although I don't particularly agree with some of her decisions in this story. I can't wait for the other series entitled <i>The Dregs</i> and set in the Grishaverse! I loved this world and I can't sulk and pout about <i>Ruin And Rising</i> forever 'cause I'd miss all the awesomesauce that those books would surely prove to be! <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-UZ9XIvMoBk8/U6aqODcD4II/AAAAAAAANl8/eXT9XgmHfBo/s1600/841bd861c7f35ebd3c5411a805c7367b.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403431739i/10092863._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For now, I'm gonna cry and rock back and forth in a corner to express my temporary unpleasure and disappointment. I'll throw a bookish tantrum. I'll drown myself in Grisha fanfics. I'll forget that this was the actual ending. I'll delete everythinggg from my brain -- except maybe the Darkling scenes that were the best, I'm telling you. I'm sad this journey is over and a bit wowed about how it all went down, but <i>The Grisha Trilogy</i> will forever hold a piece of my heart, no matter that it crushed it a bit in the end. So please go read it, because it’s still one of the best YA Fantasy stories out there.<br> <br><b>ENJOY!&lt;3</b><br><br><i>
  <b>You can also find this review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://raftul-cartilor-vampiresti.blogspot.ro/2014/06/review-ruin-and-rising-grisha-3-by.html">http://raftul-cartilor-vampiresti.blo...</a></b>
</i><br><br><b>BEFORE READING:</b><br><br>Um. No. Simply <b>NO.<br><br>A WHOLE BLOODY YEAR??? 2014?!?!</b> Leigh Bardugo has got to be kidding me!<br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-yw-sUppgTWI/UcWggAttVII/AAAAAAAALTk/1H1i6Qk1XNM/s1600/tumblr_mo0ilvUtov1s9a317o1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413355ra/813772.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Why the hell did I read the first two books before the finale is published? <i>#stupid #stupid #stupid</i><br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-GJv2DiZzfwE/UcWgG18-V7I/AAAAAAAALTU/DlsxSJ6SWQQ/s1600/blame-cry-hurt-lonely-nina-dobrey-Favim_com-374348.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413355ra/813773.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After S&amp;S I’m dying. That ending? <i>She would rise??</i> You seriously cannot end it like that. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-8SZ9lZvBe_w/UcWgLpNHLtI/AAAAAAAALTc/gXCkBQcnrt4/s1600/tumblr_inline_mkyt6rXyBt1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413355ra/813774.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oh. And Team Darkling. Always. &lt;3 I need him with Alina! Also, I hope he doesn't end up dead. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-M1B3xhuRzO0/UcWhEiP-5rI/AAAAAAAALTw/rtBqzjxY9_Q/s1600/tumblr_mmeeg4U9ww1r9habho1_500.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413355i/813775.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>P.S.</b> The author said she had started to call book 3 <i>Ruin and Racy</i>. Hot moments ahead? Please God, let it be so. Alarkling ones. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14368025970265837688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2639643797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2639643797" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2639643797?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2639643797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8856265508999919694">I actually did not hate the ending or relationship like many people told me I would. I can understand people’s frustrations with the outcome, but I felt like it made sense for the characters and, if I actually cared about them, I would be quite happy for their ending. Unfortunately, I still don’t care for anyone here, and felt like the majority of the story dragged around as we followed a “ragtag team of misfits” consisting of barely developed secondary characters led by bland main characters. N</span>
  <span id="freeText8856265508999919694" style="display:none">I actually did not hate the ending or relationship like many people told me I would. I can understand people’s frustrations with the outcome, but I felt like it made sense for the characters and, if I actually cared about them, I would be quite happy for their ending. Unfortunately, I still don’t care for anyone here, and felt like the majority of the story dragged around as we followed a “ragtag team of misfits” consisting of barely developed secondary characters led by bland main characters. Nikolai’s story arc in the second half was clearly a plot device to temporarily get him out of the picture. The Darkling remains underdeveloped as what could have been a compelling antagonist, instead reduced to a romanticized shell of a villain. Maybe I didn’t mind that the ending was anticlimactic because I was so eager for this trilogy to be over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8856265508999919694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1590456155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1590456155" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1590456155?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1590456155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4160192146041300110">I'm like a bubble of explosive happiness right now! That was incredibly perfect I can't really find the proper words!!!<br/><br/>But I'll try to anyways...........<br/><br/><br/>"What two things are infinite? The universe and the greed of men."<br/><br/><br/>This little point emphasized so much throughout this series. I adored every moment I spent reading this series. Although in my own experience I always love the first book in a series the most, because everything is so new and fresh. There is a certain giddiness associated with get</span>
  <span id="freeText4160192146041300110" style="display:none">I'm like a bubble of explosive happiness right now! That was incredibly perfect I can't really find the proper words!!!<br /><br />But I'll try to anyways...........<br /><br /><br />"What two things are infinite? The universe and the greed of men."<br /><br /><br />This little point emphasized so much throughout this series. I adored every moment I spent reading this series. Although in my own experience I always love the first book in a series the most, because everything is so new and fresh. There is a certain giddiness associated with getting to know everyone and becoming familiar with the pattern of thought of an author, better yet if you have never read the authors work before this. It's like treading into unknown territory, the excitement and the euphoria of the unknown. The last books always seem to bear a certain melancholic air about them. HOWEVER; this wasn't at all true about ruin and rising. This book is by far the best ending to a series I have ever read! And although I am a perky and expressive persona when it come to describing books in general, this book took me a level even farther. <br /><br />The story continues where siege and storm left of with a terribly rattling cliff hanger. So much tension built up around the beginning of the book that it gave me slight hand tremors at times. It's one thing to feel anticipation, it's another entirely to feel consumed or in my case suffocated by it. The best part about the two last books was Nikolai. I felt that between a charming yet eternally noble character like Mal and an indulgent yet troubled heroine like Alina, a aloof yet witty and clever character was definitely required. Although I don't particularly adore love triangles, I found the one Leigh Bardugo created wasn't the least bit perverse. It boarded well with the circumstances and only aided in further complicating the decisions and sacrifices. <br /><br />The dark humor however probably did me best. It was the perfect combination of inappropriate and contrary. There is nothing like the threat of imminent death and destruction hanging over ones head to make you feel like you should use every possible moment. The way the story unfurled its wings and began to soar was inexplicably delightful. <br /><br />"He’d wanted me to believe in his ruthlessness.<br />Then I remembered his words from so long ago: Make me your villain."<br /><br />There are many villains, every story needs a villain truly. In this series however I rooted for the villain maybe more than once. The darkling was a uniquely meticulous character, one that although devious and evil per say, was burdened by the eternity of loneliness. Some characters are meant to be hated, but for me the darkling had a right to empathy. Bardugo created a character carefully drawn between the lines of good and bad, a perfect shade of grey.<br /><br />Overall I think it's needless to say I loved everything about this book. The way the author allowed the characters to build their alternate realities of what could have been like the shared story moments in the abandoned house just before the outbreak of war, or the third person BEFORE and AFTERS that started and ended every book. The last after actually brought a mist to my eyes, the good kind of pain. The types that stings your heart but fills it with a sad kind of joy. I so loved this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4160192146041300110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It belongs to us.” Then he set down the rifle and wiped his hands on a rag.</b></i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498737898ra/23157641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4)<i><b>“Know that I loved you,” she said to the Darkling. “Know that it was not enough.”</b></i><br>I liked Baghra!! Deep down she was so good person! She helped Alina so many times but she loved her son deeply but at the end it wasn't enough.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487177784ra/21984264.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5)I am so glad that Alina lost her powers because we all saw what they did to the Darkling!<br><br><i><b>"I couldn’t forget what he’d done, and I wouldn’t forgive what he was: a murderer. A monster. A man who had tortured my friends and slaughtered the people I’d tried to protect."</b></i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493322402ra/22604237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6)<i><b>“Alina, this is the alliance I want: the First and Second Armies brought together. As for the rest, I’ve always known that whatever marriage I made would be political. It would be about power, not love. But we might get lucky. In time, we might have both.”<br>“Or the third amplifier will turn me into a power-mad dictator and you’ll have to kill me.”<br> “Yes, that would make for an awkward honeymoon.”</b></i><br><br>Nikolai!!! He is so funny! I rally really like him! If Mal didn't exist, I would want Nikolai to be with Alina! Okay he likes her and she likes him but that wouldn't last!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498055801ra/23085995.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>7)<i><b>“I wasn’t afraid of you, Alina.   <i>“Maybe love was superstition, a prayer we said to keep the truth of loneliness at bay."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Why you should read the Grisha trilogy:<br/><br/>1. The Darkling<br/>2. Mal <br/>3. Pirates and demons and magical birds<br/>4. The Darkling<br/>5. Nikolai<br/>6. The Darkling<br/>7. Mal and Alina<br/>8. Mal<br/>9. MAL<br/>10. Malyen Fucking Oretsev<br/><br/>If you haven't gotten it yet, I'm kind of in love with Mal. And I know some people preferred the other heroes</span>
  <span id="freeText15817488495241942955" style="display:none">THIS SERIES IS BEING TURNED INTO A NETFLIX SERIES AND HOLY SHIT MY EXCITEMENT CAN NOT BE CONTAINED!!!!!!! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474497383i/20607922._SY540_.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Maybe love was superstition, a prayer we said to keep the truth of loneliness at bay."</i>
</b><br><br>Why you should read the Grisha trilogy:<br><br>1. The Darkling<br>2. Mal <br>3. Pirates and demons and magical birds<br>4. The Darkling<br>5. Nikolai<br>6. The Darkling<br>7. Mal and Alina<br>8. Mal<br>9. MAL<br>10. Malyen Fucking Oretsev<br><br>If you haven't gotten it yet, I'm kind of in love with Mal. And I know some people preferred the other heroes over him. Maybe because he wasn't as funny as Nikolai or as seductive as the Darkling. But I loved that boy from the start and Chapter 16 and the epilogue ruined my life. I read them 4 times. And I think when I'm done writing this review I'm going back to read them again.<br><br>What I also loved: how I was oddly okay with any way this could have ended. I actually kept going back and forth with how I wanted the story to conclude. Towards the last half, I HOPED it would end a certain way. I was PRAYING Alina would end up with a certain someone. And I can honestly say the ending was just perfection. <b>PER-FREAKING-FECTION.</b> I cried and weeped and laughed and I just thought it couldn't have been better.<br><br>The characters were realistic, fantastic, and fun. The plot twists were <b>CRAZY</b>. The Darkling is literally the most fascinating and intriguing character I have read about and I can't praise Leigh enough for creating someone like him. For creating this whole series that stayed true to its characters and theme from the very beginning. And for Mal. Thank you for Mal.<br><br>Fav quotes:<br><br><b>
  <i>"In the end, maybe love just meant longing for something impossibly bright and forever out of reach."<br><br>"I am not ruined. I am ruination."<br><br>"I will strip away all that you know, all that you love, until you have no shelter but me."<br><br>"I would have been different too, without you. Weaker, reckless." He smiled slightly. "Afraid of the dark." He brushed the tears from my cheeks. I wasn't sure when they'd started. "But no matter who or what I was, I would have been yours."<br><br>"You are all I ever wanted. You are the whole of my heart."<br><br>"When evening fell, the boy would bring the girl a glass of tea, a slice of lemon cake, an apple blossom floating in a blue cup. He would kiss her neck and whisper new names in her ear: beauty, beloved, cherished, my heart.<br>They had an ordinary life, full of ordinary things - if love can ever be called that."</i>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8503045740173717397"><i>This is the way the world ends. Not with a bang but a whimper. <br/>T.S. Eliot</i><br/><br/>What a perfect encapsulation of this miserable conclusion. <br/><br/>I thought I had prepared myself mentally for the worst of scenarios. Even as I prayed desperately for a satisfying ending to my favorite YA series of all time, I readied myself for every possible emotion: For devastation. For despair. For my soul to be raked over the coals until it became a shriveled, blackened thing so that I could never feel happiness again. <br/><br/>I was</span>
  <span id="freeText8503045740173717397" style="display:none"><i>This is the way the world ends. Not with a bang but a whimper. <br>T.S. Eliot</i><br><br>What a perfect encapsulation of this miserable conclusion. <br><br>I thought I had prepared myself mentally for the worst of scenarios. Even as I prayed desperately for a satisfying ending to my favorite YA series of all time, I readied myself for every possible emotion: For devastation. For despair. For my soul to be raked over the coals until it became a shriveled, blackened thing so that I could never feel happiness again. <br><br>I was definitely not ready to feel like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381528767ra/4986510.gif" width="200" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because that ending was BAD. It wasn't simply controversial, or polarizing, or provocative. It was just plain <i>bad</i>. It was half-cooked, it was predictable, it was unoriginal, it was poorly-plotted, it was the epitome of YA gone tame and lame. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I have so many grievances against this book that I can hardly list them all. But foremost on the list is definitely the BUTCHERING OF THE DARKLING. Over and over again, we've been told that the Darkling is a morally ambiguous character, whose actions can be categorized as neither right nor wrong. And yet all we see of him in R+R is his committing atrocity after atrocity! Was it so that when he met his pitiful end, we'd feel that he "deserved" it? What I had looked forward to the most was gleaning further insight into his character, but there was no more insight to be gained, because in the book he ONLY APPEARS ABOUT ~5 TIMES. In the previous installments, he was enigmatic and mysterious. Here, he's just a half-baked character that the author didn't bother to flesh out. <br><br>His pitiful excuse for a death scene deserves a rant all of its own. A knife to the heart? WTF? Why not just have him choke to death on a chicken bone? Both endings would carry the same dignity for a man of his power. Just a pathetic and lazy copout. "Freed from his misery" "a merciful death" etc, MY BUTT. He was put down like a DOG. <br><br>And of course, the most grievious wound of them all. Alina. Losing her powers. AGAIN. To return to the orphanage. With Mal. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395026216ra/8937157.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm speechless with the inanity of it all.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>To reverse all of the protagonist's hardwon character development, and to lazily discard the best pairing (and most captivating individual) in one fell swoop...what a complete and utter disappointment. The takeaway message here? It's okay for a woman to repress her potential for the sake of her man. After all, ordinary love triumphs over all, so girls! Keep your talents on the down-low, otherwise you might make your boyfriend feel "inferior!" <br><br>I expected so much more out of the author. This was my favorite trilogy, this was my adored OTP, and it was all blown to smithereens in a whimper of an ending. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393675247ra/8750500.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so angry. Given the lack of strong female protagonists in YA, and the dearth of supportive love interests, why on Earth would an author doom her character to this circular end? </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks">Grace (BURTSBOOKS)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096101571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3546229118045238780">3.5 stars <br/><br/>Book Stockholm syndrome took me hostage with this series and now that it's over I don't know what to do. I started off this series not caring at all and by the middle of this third book I was sobbing on my kitchen floor. I guess you could say the series got better as it went along. I’m not sure about that but I do know half this book ripped my heart out. The other half pissed me off but if you read my review’s of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101672?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'> Shadow and Bone </a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101706?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1#comment_form' rel='nofollow noopener'>Siege and Storm</a> that isn’t exactly rare for this se</span>
  <span id="freeText3546229118045238780" style="display:none">3.5 stars <br /><br />Book Stockholm syndrome took me hostage with this series and now that it's over I don't know what to do. I started off this series not caring at all and by the middle of this third book I was sobbing on my kitchen floor. I guess you could say the series got better as it went along. I’m not sure about that but I do know half this book ripped my heart out. The other half pissed me off but if you read my review’s of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101672?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shadow and Bone </a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101706?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1#comment_form" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> that isn’t exactly rare for this series. <br /><br />The rest of this is gonna be a mess of unorganized spoilers. This is your warning. <br /><br />So, obviously, the most important part of this series is Nikolai (some people argue that it’s Alina and Mal’s relationship but lol let’s be real). I, like everyone else that has read these books, love him and he was, of course, the cause of my sobbing on my kitchen floor that I mentioned earlier. He was the most interesting and devastating part of this book series and I will forever be bitter about the shit he had to go through in this book. I know he didn’t have to kill the love of his life or anything but arguably he had the biggest struggle of any character in this series with that bullshit The Darkling did to him and it hurts my heart. Also because of The Darkling’s stupid treachery, Nikolai wasn’t nearly as present in the story as he should have been and I’m bitter. Where is the Nikolai trilogy???? I need it immediately. I need more Nikolai content after this drought of a book. <br /><br />Anyway, moving on. I really enjoyed that a lot of the characters that were mostly background in the previous two books really came to life in this book. Zoya and David ended up being hilarious characters and I totally didn’t see that coming. <br /><br />I still don’t get why everyone loves The Darkling. I mean half the time he made me want to rip my hair out and Alina killing him was possibly the best thing that happened the entire series but also he’s a really interesting antagonist and I begrudgingly admit that reading this story from his point of view would’ve been enthralling. I mean just imagine for a second: this story being told by him instead of Alina. Like damn that would change everything. <br /><br />Speaking of Alina, maybe I should talk about her and by extension Mal. Here we are, you all saw it coming. I can’t simply talk about this series without talking about how utterly uninterested I am in Alina and Mal’s romance. It’s just boring and overdone idk man. <br /><br />The worst part is I really enjoyed the concept of Mal as the third amplifier, I totally didn’t see it coming and it made me feel actual emotions towards their relationship. Like I was actually worried for Mal. Can you believe it? Idk maybe it makes me fucked up but I’m a sucker for sacrifices like that and the angst surrounding it was the perfect mix of satisfying and heartbreaking. <br /><br />I honestly didn’t think Alina had it in her to kill Mal but she did and I was super impressed and upset and just satisfied with the story being done so well. You can imagine how cheated I felt when Mal suddenly was coming back to life. Like hello????? I’m still confused about how that even happened. Also, it was super annoying and convenient that Alina lost her powers just like Mal had always wanted. Oh yay, they can be together now! Yes, that was exactly what I wanted from this book! Ugh, I feel played. <br /><br />Other than that little fact, I thought this book was great and it put me on an emotional roller coaster, which sadly I don’t get to experience much in my reading life. I’m happy I finally read this trilogy. I finally feel like I’m part of the club and I’m ready to move on to Six of Crows. The grisha verse is a rich, captivating world. The politics are super dark and twisted but so interesting to read about and I can’t wait for Leigh Bardugo to pull a Cassandra Clare and just continue this world forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3546229118045238780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I also want to highlight characters like Bagrah, Nikolai, Tamar, Tolya, Genya, David &amp; Zoya, all unique and indispensable for the plot, without them this story wouldn't be the same.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KRBzcIhEx28xztWTwY6AX2jbJ3ihodiL6U/VOdsCJX+04w9cd8NY3nGrusI2qdMpg3sWGDLIX3OT7huVTB3i+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RcO9VoOlKpkWObA6Nt0YFEYxFGQtkeGvg5zioU4hL5XYMMF6fCK1KFZc32vB+ktirZElBL74Zlf5PSwN2T7oEg==')})
  }

Yet she has sworn an oath to assist those in need—and will honor it. But Lord Westfall carries shadows from his own past, and Yrene soon comes to realize they could engulf them both.\n\nIn this sweeping parallel novel to the New York Times bestselling Empire of Storms, Chaol, Nesryn, and Yrene will have to draw on every scrap of their resilience if they wish to save their friends. But while they become entangled in the political webs of the khaganate, deep in the shadows of mighty mountains where warriors soar on legendary ruks, long-awaited answers slumber. <span id="freeTextContainer16256938511557418640">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction & Fantasy. Her other works include Wo</span>
  <span id="freeText16256938511557418640" style="display:none">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy. Her other works include Wonder Woman: Warbringer and Ninth House (Goodreads Choice Winner for Best Fantasy 2019) which is being developed for television by Amazon Studios. Leigh was born in Jerusalem, grew up in Southern California, and graduated from Yale University. These days she lives and writes in Los Angeles. For information on new releases and appearances, sign up for her <a href="https://https//leighbardugo.us11.list-manage.com/subscribe?u=160b0462d4826c60dbb8af320&amp;id=ec014907b2" rel="nofollow noopener">newsletter</a>.<br /><br />She would be delighted if you followed her on <a href="http://twitter.com/Lbardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, elated if you visited her at <a href="http://leighbardugo.com" rel="nofollow noopener">LeighBardugo.com</a>, and fairly giddy if you liked her selfies on <a href="http://instagram.com/lbardugo/7" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>. <br /><br /></span>
